- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls

# LLVM SelectionDAG Assertion Failure Diagnosis

## Your Task

A production build system using LLVM is crashing with the error: 'Cannot expand this type; LLVM lacks the right hooks'. Trace this assertion to its source in `llvm/llvm-project`. Find: 1. The C++ source file in `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/` that contains this error message or assertion. 2. The function in that file where the assertion fires (look for type legalization expansion logic). 3. The header file that defines the `EVT` (Extended Value Type) class and its `isSimple()` method (look in `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/`). 4. The file that defines the `LegalizeDAG` class which orchestrates type legalization and may call the expand function. Report the repo, file path, and function or class name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `github.com/llvm/llvm-project` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `github.com/gcc-mirror/gcc` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

**2. EVT Class Definition**

- **Method**: `EVT::isSimple()` (lines 137-139)
- Tests whether a type is simple vs. extended

- **File**: `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeTypes.h`
- **Class**: `DAGTypeLegalizer` (line 31)

**4. Type Conversion Logic**
- **File**: `llvm/lib/CodeGen/TargetLoweringBase.cpp`

It transforms\\n10: // an arbitrary well-formed SelectionDAG to only consist of legal types.  This\\n11: // is common code shared among the LegalizeTypes*.cpp files.\\n12: //\\n13: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n14: \\n15: #include \\\"LegalizeTypes.h\\\"\\n16: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/SetVector.h\\\"\\n17: #include \\\"llvm/IR/DataLayout.h\\\"\\n18: #include \\\"llvm/Support/CommandLine.h\\\"\\n19: #include \\\"llvm/Support/ErrorHandling.h\\\"\\n20: #include \\\"llvm/Support/raw_ostream.h\\\"\\n21: using namespace llvm;\\n22: \\n23: #define DEBUG_TYPE \\\"legalize-types\\\"\\n24: \\n25: static cl::opt<bool>\\n26: EnableExpensiveChecks(\\\"enable-legalize-types-checking\\\", cl::Hidden);\\n27: \\n28: /// Do extensive, expensive, basic correctness checking.\\n29: void DAGTypeLegalizer::PerformExpensiveChecks() {\\n30:   // If a node is not processed, then none of its values should be mapped by any\\n31:   // of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\\n32: \\n33:   // If a node is processed, then each value with an illegal type must be mapped\\n34:   // by exactly one of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\\n35:   // Values with a legal type may be mapped by ReplacedValues, but not by any of\\n36:   // the other maps.\\n37: \\n38:   // Note that these invariants may not hold momentarily when processing a node:\\n39:   // the node being processed may be put in a map before being marked Processed.\\n40: \\n41:   // Note that it is possible to have nodes marked NewNode in the DAG.  This can\\n42:   // occur in two ways.  Firstly, a node may be created during legalization but\\n43:   // never passed to the legalization core.  This is usually due to the implicit\\n44:   // folding that occurs when using the DAG.getNode operators.  Secondly, a new\\n45:   // node may be passed to the legalization core, but when analyzed may morph\\n46:   // into a different node, leaving the original node as a NewNode in the DAG.\\n47:   // A node may morph if one of its operands changes during analysis.  Whether\\n48:   // it actually morphs or not depends on whether, after updating its operands,\\n49:   // it is equivalent to an existing node: if so, it morphs into that existing\\n50:   // node (CSE).  An operand can change during analysis if the operand is a new\\n51:   // node that morphs, or it is a processed value that was mapped to some other\\n52:   // value (as recorded in ReplacedValues) in which case the operand is turned\\n53:   // into that other value.  If a node morphs then the node it morphed into will\\n54:   // be used instead of it for legalization, however the original node continues\\n55:   // to live on in the DAG.\\n56:   // The conclusion is that though there may be nodes marked NewNode in the DAG,\\n57:   // all uses of such nodes are also marked NewNode: the result is a fungus of\\n58:   // NewNodes growing on top of the useful nodes, and perhaps using them, but\\n59:   // not used by them.\\n60: \\n61:   // If a value is mapped by ReplacedValues, then it must have no uses, except\\n62:   // by nodes marked NewNode (see above).\\n63: \\n64:   // The final node obtained by mapping by ReplacedValues is not marked NewNode.\\n65:   // Note that ReplacedValues should be applied iteratively.\\n66: \\n67:   // Note that the ReplacedValues map may also map deleted nodes (by iterating\\n68:   // over the DAG we never dereference deleted nodes).  This means that it may\\n69:   // also map nodes marked NewNode if the deallocated memory was reallocated as\\n70:   // another node, and that new node was not seen by the LegalizeTypes machinery\\n71:   // (for example because it was created but not used).  In general, we cannot\\n72:   // distinguish between new nodes and deleted nodes.\\n73:   SmallVector<SDNode*, 16> NewNodes;\\n74:   for (SDNode &Node : DAG.allnodes()) {\\n75:     // Remember nodes marked NewNode - they are subject to extra checking below.\\n76:     if (Node.getNodeId() == NewNode)\\n77:       NewNodes.push_back(&Node);\\n78: \\n79:     for (unsigned i = 0, e = Node.getNumValues(); i != e; ++i) {\\n80:       SDValue Res(&Node, i);\\n81:       bool Failed = false;\\n82:       // Don't create a value in map.\\n83:       auto ResId = ValueToIdMap.lookup(Res);\\n84: \\n85:       unsigned Mapped = 0;\\n86:       if (ResId) {\\n87:         auto I = ReplacedValues.find(ResId);\\n88:         if (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\\n89:           Mapped |= 1;\\n90:           // Check that remapped values are only used by nodes marked NewNode.\\n91:           for (SDUse &U : Node.uses())\\n92:             if (U.getResNo() == i)\\n93:               assert(U.getUser()->getNodeId() == NewNode &&\\n94:                      \\\"Remapped value has non-trivial use!\\\");\\n95: \\n96:           // Check that the final result of applying ReplacedValues is not\\n97:           // marked NewNode.\\n98:           auto NewValId = I->second;\\n99:           I = ReplacedValues.find(NewValId);\\n100:           while (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/llvm/llvm-project@ab0823c9c765972ab62497391df96b10e5b4471f/-/blob/llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeTypes.cpp%3FL1-100\"}",

    "content": "1: //===-- LegalizeTypes.cpp - Common code for DAG type legalizer ------------===//\n2: //\n3: // Part of the LLVM Project, under the Apache License v2.0 with LLVM Exceptions.\n4: // See https://llvm.org/LICENSE.txt for license information.\n5: // SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 WITH LLVM-exception\n6: //\n7: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n8: //\n9: // This file implements the SelectionDAG::LegalizeTypes method.  It transforms\n10: // an arbitrary well-formed SelectionDAG to only consist of legal types.  This\n11: // is common code shared among the LegalizeTypes*.cpp files.\n12: //\n13: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n14: \n15: #include \"LegalizeTypes.h\"\n16: #include \"llvm/ADT/SetVector.h\"\n17: #include \"llvm/IR/DataLayout.h\"\n18: #include \"llvm/Support/CommandLine.h\"\n19: #include \"llvm/Support/ErrorHandling.h\"\n20: #include \"llvm/Support/raw_ostream.h\"\n21: using namespace llvm;\n22: \n23: #define DEBUG_TYPE \"legalize-types\"\n24: \n25: static cl::opt<bool>\n26: EnableExpensiveChecks(\"enable-legalize-types-checking\", cl::Hidden);\n27: \n28: /// Do extensive, expensive, basic correctness checking.\n29: void DAGTypeLegalizer::PerformExpensiveChecks() {\n30:   // If a node is not processed, then none of its values should be mapped by any\n31:   // of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\n32: \n33:   // If a node is processed, then each value with an illegal type must be mapped\n34:   // by exactly one of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\n35:   // Values with a legal type may be mapped by ReplacedValues, but not by any of\n36:   // the other maps.\n37: \n38:   // Note that these invariants may not hold momentarily when processing a node:\n39:   // the node being processed may be put in a map before being marked Processed.\n40: \n41:   // Note that it is possible to have nodes marked NewNode in the DAG.  This can\n42:   // occur in two ways.  Firstly, a node may be created during legalization but\n43:   // never passed to the legalization core.  This is usually due to the implicit\n44:   // folding that occurs when using the DAG.getNode operators.  Secondly, a new\n45:   // node may be passed to the legalization core, but when analyzed may morph\n46:   // into a different node, leaving the original node as a NewNode in the DAG.\n47:   // A node may morph if one of its operands changes during analysis.  Whether\n48:   // it actually morphs or not depends on whether, after updating its operands,\n49:   // it is equivalent to an existing node: if so, it morphs into that existing\n50:   // node (CSE).  An operand can change during analysis if the operand is a new\n51:   // node that morphs, or it is a processed value that was mapped to some other\n52:   // value (as recorded in ReplacedValues) in which case the operand is turned\n53:   // into that other value.  If a node morphs then the node it morphed into will\n54:   // be used instead of it for legalization, however the original node continues\n55:   // to live on in the DAG.\n56:   // The conclusion is that though there may be nodes marked NewNode in the DAG,\n57:   // all uses of such nodes are also marked NewNode: the result is a fungus of\n58:   // NewNodes growing on top of the useful nodes, and perhaps using them, but\n59:   // not used by them.\n60: \n61:   // If a value is mapped by ReplacedValues, then it must have no uses, except\n62:   // by nodes marked NewNode (see above).\n63: \n64:   // The final node obtained by mapping by ReplacedValues is not marked NewNode.\n65:   // Note that ReplacedValues should be applied iteratively.\n66: \n67:   // Note that the ReplacedValues map may also map deleted nodes (by iterating\n68:   // over the DAG we never dereference deleted nodes).  This means that it may\n69:   // also map nodes marked NewNode if the deallocated memory was reallocated as\n70:   // another node, and that new node was not seen by the LegalizeTypes machinery\n71:   // (for example because it was created but not used).  In general, we cannot\n72:   // distinguish between new nodes and deleted nodes.\n73:   SmallVector<SDNode*, 16> NewNodes;\n74:   for (SDNode &Node : DAG.allnodes()) {\n75:     // Remember nodes marked NewNode - they are subject to extra checking below.\n76:     if (Node.getNodeId() == NewNode)\n77:       NewNodes.push_back(&Node);\n78: \n79:     for (unsigned i = 0, e = Node.getNumValues(); i != e; ++i) {\n80:       SDValue Res(&Node, i);\n81:       bool Failed = false;\n82:       // Don't create a value in map.\n83:       auto ResId = ValueToIdMap.lookup(Res);\n84: \n85:       unsigned Mapped = 0;\n86:       if (ResId) {\n87:         auto I = ReplacedValues.find(ResId);\n88:         if (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\n89:           Mapped |= 1;\n90:           // Check that remapped values are only used by nodes marked NewNode.\n91:           for (SDUse &U : Node.uses())\n92:             if (U.getResNo() == i)\n93:               assert(U.getUser()->getNodeId() == NewNode &&\n94:                      \"Remapped value has non-trivial use!\");\n95: \n96:           // Check that the final result of applying ReplacedValues is not\n97:           // marked NewNode.\n98:           auto NewValId = I->second;\n99:           I = ReplacedValues.find(NewValId);\n100:           while (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\n101: ",
